Most STs also allow a few seconds for day abilities between the execution and officially declaring the day over and night beginning, but that might vary by ST, so players should clarify what is allowable before relying on that window. Most would not allow the Slayer their shot after their execution as they are dead.

If the Slayer kills the Demon will there still be nominations that day?

If the game ends, then there will be no nominations. If the game continues, say due to a Scarlet Woman, nominations continue as normal.

Can the Slayer shoot mid vote?

Yes, but the ST might want to finish resolving the vote first and the player may have repeat their target in case the ST did not hear it or forgot. The ST may not be inclined to let the Slayer kill or clear someone in the middle of the vote, so the Slayer might want to do it before, so that there is no need to vote, or after, to convince town to lift.

The evil Snake Charmer charms a good Demon, swapping roles. Do they still swap alignments?

Yes.

If the Snake Charmer charms the Demon, do they receive any bluffs?

No.

What happens when the Cannibal Snake Charmer picks the Demon?

The Cannibal becomes an evil Demon and the Demon becomes a good poisoned Cannibal. The Demon is not told that they are poisoned but will deduce that they Cannibal SC picked them.

If the dead self-poisoning Snake Charmer is resurrected (Professor / Al-Hadikhia) are they now healthy?

Yes, as they are treated as a new instance of the character.

If the Snake Charmer and the Demon swap, does the new Demon learn who the Minions are?

No, unless the Poppy Grower is killed after that.

Can the ST show a poisoned Snake Charmer that she turned into the evil Demon?

Yes, but it is not recommended. The ST can even give a fake Lunatic, tell her the next night that she killed the Poppy Grower, ...

If the Snake Charmer chooses a dead demon, does she become the Demon?

The Snake Charmer must choose alive players.

The Snake Charmer picks the Pukka. Does the old Pukka's pick from the previous night get nullified so there are no deaths this night?

Yes.

What is the difference between the Demon being picked by the Snake Charmer and the Philosopher Snake Charmer?

In the first case the Demon becomes a self-poisoned Snake Charmer, while in the second case she becomes a self-poisoned Philosopher.

What happens if the Snake Charmer hits the Lleech?

The ST needs to shuffle a lot of tokens:

  1. The Snake Charmer becomes the new Lleech.
  2. The ex-Lleech becomes the poisoned Snake Charmer.
  3. The previous host is no longer poisoned or a host, so the host token is removed.
  4. The new Lleech, just as if it was N1, gets to pick a new host.

Does the new Demon wake and kill after a Snake Charmer swap?

Yes, assuming their Demon character wakes that night, since they are after the SC on the night order.

The Philosopher picks Snake Charmer, philo-drunking the original SC, and then chooses the Demon. So the starting Philo is now the evil Demon and the starting Demon is now the poisoned good Philo. What happens when the original no longer Philo-drunk Snake Charmer chooses this new demon?

In the case of a Snake Charmer and a Philosopher with the Snake Charmer ability both in play, the ST decides who acts first, which is important for this question.

If the Philosopher-SC acts first and becomes the Demon, then the old Demon becomes a poisoned Philosopher and the actual SC becomes sober (Why would the original Snake Charmer become sober? Because the Philo causing them to be drunk is no longer in play; we have a new instance of the Philo) Now the Snake Charmer can also choose the new Demon (the game's starting Philo) and swap to the Demon ... giving the possibility of one player (the OG Philosopher) going from good Philo to evil Demon to good self poisoned SC. What happens to the OG demon (who became the self poisioned Philo)? The original Demon would still be the self poisoned Philosopher, the second snake charming would not change that.

Depending on the kind of game the ST likes to run and the group of players would like to experience, generally it would be recommended to have the Philo-drunk Snake Charmer choose first to prevent this overload of shenanigans.

Can the Minions learn evil characters via the Snitch?

Yes, if the ST wants that. The Snitch's text does not specify "good characters‚Äù.

How does the Marionette jinx with the Snitch work?

The Marionette is not woken to learn three out of play characters. Instead the Demon is shown an additional three instead, with additional meaning just that: the Demon must see three more different characters. But, Snitch bluffs do not have to be good roles; useful if the ST think the Demon is good as is, or is running out of tokens for a full game.

Does the Soldier who is safe from the Demon still die when they are stabbed by the Assassin holding Lil' Monsta?

Yes. Their death does seem consistent with the Assassin's ability.

Minions killed by the Vigormortis poison a Townsfolk neighbour. Is the Soldier safe from this poisoning?

Yes, as it is a Demon ability that causes the poisoning.

Can the sober Soldier die during the night in a Lil' Monsta game?

Not to the Lil' Monsta or the babysitter, as the source of the kill is still the Demon even when the ST picks the target. It is possible for the Soldier to die to non Demon sources.

Can the soldier die in a Legion game?

Not to Legion, as a Legion player counts as both a Demon and a Minion, and the source of the kill is still a Legion player even when the ST picks the target.

Is the Soldier safe from the Demon using the Barber swap on them?

No.

If the Soldier is sitting next to the No Dashii, they are not poisoned since they are safe from the Demon. However if they are ever drunked or poisoned from another source (Poisoner / Sailor / ...), they get No Dashii poisoned. Once the drunking or poisoning wears off, is the Soldier still No Dashii poisoned?

Yes.

The Soldier is safe from the No Dashii's poison, but is she also safe from the Pukka poison and the subsequent kill?

Yes, and she is also immune to the Lleech's poison, but is still the host, just an unpoisoned host.

The Soldier is safe from the No Dashii poison. Does the poisoning pass through the Soldier to the next Townsfolk?

No, the No Dashii only ever skips non-Townsfolk players. If the neighbouring Townsfolk player is immune in some way, like the Soldier, then the poisoning simply stops and has no effect.

Can the Spy be poisoned by the No Dashii?

No. The poisoning would sort of loop:

  1. The Spy who neighbours the No Dashii and misregisters as a Townsfolk becomes poisoned.
  2. Being poisoned, the Spy can no longer register as a Townsfolk.
  3. The No Dashii poisoning must move to the next neighbour as the current target is not a Townsfolk so no longer valid.
  4. The Spy is no longer poisoned and regains their ability.

But the ST is free to repeatedly move the poison from the Spy to the next Townsfolk and back, to their own delight for as long as they want.

Can the Spy registering as good become the Farmer?

Yes.

Can the Spy register as not a Minion and stay as the Spy despite an attempted Engineer swap?

Yes.

If the Ojo or the Courtier chose the Spy, could the Spy misregister to avoid being chosen?

Yes.

If the Ojo targets a Townsfolk can the attack be redirected to the Spy registering as same?

Yes but don't.

The Spy misregistering as a good character can cause her:

  • to die instead when the Ojo targets any good character.
  • to survive if the Ojo targets the Spy, causing an Ojo miss so the ST picks the kill(s).

But note:

  • if the Spy does register as the intended target there is still only one death, so the ST could not kill off both the actual target and the Spy.
  • the Spy could still register as the Spy and be killed by the Ojo.

This logic also works with the Recluse:

  • picking any evil character can kill the Recluse instead
  • picking the Recluse can have the Recluse misregister and therefore survive

If the Spy is drunk / poisoned, does she still get to view the Grimoire or does she get to view a fake version of the Grimoire?

The ST could show the drunk / poisoned Spy any version of the Grimoire that they wished:

  • the correct one,
  • something totally wild,
  • the Grimoire with just one or two small changes to throw off what the Spy thinks the gamestate is.

Since showing her the correct Grimoire works against the idea of the Spy malfunctioning, and showing her a wildly inaccurate Grimoire tips her off that she is getting bad info, the simpler approach is just to show her that different people are malfunctioning, then watch her report that the Mayor or the Slayer is powerless, and then surprise!

Remember that the Spy cannot misregister as a Townsfolk or Outsider while drunk or poisoned.

When showing the (healthy and sober) Spy the Grimoire, can the ST replace a (healthy and sober) Recluse's token with any Minion or Demon token, and/or the Spy's own token with any Townsfolk or Outsider token? For example, could you replace the Spy's own token with the Drunk token for funs and giggles?

Yes, and it is used sometimes, for example, to show what the Spy was seen as to the Washerwoman or the Librarian.

When the Spy sees the Grimoire, is it just the roles or also the reminder tokens used?

It is whatever the ST has in the Grimoire at the time really. They can remove the reminder tokens if they want, but most STs leave them in.

Can the Spy be the Red Herring?

Yes, though it is kinda sneaky. The Spy can also start registering as evil at some point, causing the RH to move to another good player (even sneakier). Use caution.

Could nominating the Spy who is registering as the Virgin cause the nominator to be executed?

No. Registering as something does not give that player the ability.

Can the Spy register as the Damsel and then the Recluse be told that the Damsel is in play?

No. The Spy registering as a role does not gain that role's ability.

Can the sober and healthy Slayer hit the Spy, who registeres as the Recluse, which then registers as the Demon?

No. Registering as something does not give the player that ability. So the Spy registering as the Recluse cannot then register through the Recluse's ability, since they do not have it.

If the Spy is juggled twice, once as the Spy and once as the Juggler, can the Juggler receive a two, or can the Spy only register as one character for the whole ability?

0, 1 and 2 are all valid numbers for that juggle. Comparing with the Spy/Chef interaction, getting a two is valid. But, just because an ST could give a two, does not mean that she should.

If the Spy is preached and later dies, do they get the misregistration part of their ability back after the Preacher dies?

Yes.

Can the Town Crier can get a no if the Spy nominates?

Yes.

Is it okay to show the Washerwoman an out of play Townsfolk and point to the Spy and one other player?

It is legal to do that with the Washerwoman and Librarian, and show no real Minions to the Investigator using the Recluse. This could be a good move for the ST when there is not a lot of other misinformation in play, for instance, no Drunk and no Poisoner.

What happens if the Steward's good player becomes evil later?

Nothing. The Steward is a start knowing ability, not a constantly knows.

Can the Fang Gu jump to a Storm Caught Outsider?

No, as the Fang Gu must be able to kill their target in order to jump to them.

If the player favoured by the Storm Catcher is turned evil (Mezepheles) what happens?

They are still storm caught meaning they can only die by execution.

If the Boomdandy explodes, can the player favoured by the Storm Catcher die?

No. However, the Storm Catcher can be removed from play immediately before the Boomdandy execution and kill the previously storm caught character at will.

The Storm Catcher favours the Damsel ...?

Do not storm catch the Damsel!

Do newly created evil players, such as the Demon jumping, learn the player favoured by the Storm Catcher?

Yes.

Does the Marionette learn the player favoured by the Storm Catcher?

It would probably be best not to, as otherwise that would tell the Marionette that they are evil. Good players do not learn about storm caught players, and the Marionette thinks they are good, so that kind of works.

Does an evil player who becomes the Sweetheart still drunk another player when they die?

Yes.

The Sweetheart dies and drunks a player. Does the player sober if they ever change character?

No. The Sweetheart drunkness is on the player, not the character, so the new character enters play drunk. To stop the drunking would require the Sweetheart to be swapped.

If a dead player becomes the Sweetheart (Pit-Hag / Barber swap / ...) is another player Sweetheart drunked for the rest of the game?

No.

The Sweetheart's ability is a trigger on death, not a constant check of living status, as it states "when you die" not "whilst you are dead", so:

  • a player with the Sweetheart ability dies: another player is instantly drunked for the rest of the game
  • a dead player becomes the Sweetheart: no drunking happens.

If the Sweetheart is resurrected (Al-Hadikhia) or swapped to a living player, so that there is now a living Sweetheart in the game, does the player that they previously drunked become sober?

Yes.

Resurrected and swapped roles are treated as new instances of the role, so as a new instance of the Sweetheart, any drunking by the previous instance ceases. If the new instance dies, then a player is drunked again.

Can either of the Tea Lady's good neighbours die to the Moon Child?

No.

If both of the Tea Lady's neighbours are good then they cannot die to any ability except the Assassin's.

What happens if the Tea Lady has two good neighbours and a multi-kill demon (Shabaloth / Po / ...) attacks the Tea Lady and one or both of her neighbours? Does her protection go away when she is attacked or does it last that night until dawn?

As soon as the Tea Lady dies, the protection disappears. The Demon's choice order matters though. If the protected TL neighbour is chosen first and then the TL is chosen, only the TL dies. But if the TL is chosen first, the protection is gone and the neighbour will also die.

If the Tea Lady's neighbours are a two good players, one of whom is a Traveller, can that Traveller be exiled?

No, exile is death and the Tea Lady protects their neighbours from dying. The Traveller can leave the game, though.

Does the Tea Lady ability ignore neighbouring Travellers?

No.

Can the Tea Lady protect a Traveller from exile?

Yes. Exiles are death, and the Tea Lady protects her neighbours from death.

Can the Tinker die by execution if they are protected, for example by a Tea Lady?

No.

Can the Tinker die in the day due to their power?

Yes, as long as they are able to die and are not protected by another ability. But although you can, but you probably should not.

It is legal for the ST to kill the Tinker at the start of the day when night deaths are announced, to hide the fact that they died during the day. In BMR that can give the Godfather a kill or frame an Assassin kill if they were Innkept.

Suppose the Tinker cannot die at night due to Innkeeper protection, but the ST kills them immediately at dawn to make the town think they died at night. Is the ST obligated to specify whether or not they died "at night", which is something a lot of STs do?

RAW the ST can wait a fraction of a second after announcing night deaths and then say the Tinker died, There is no need to specify if it was a night death or not.

If the Town Crier is dead during the day and resurrected the next night (Al-Hadikhia / Professor / ...), are they told if a Minion nominated the previous day?

Yes.

Does the Demon get bluffs in a Teensyville game?

No. Also the evil team does not learn each other.

Unless it is a Teensyville script using the Toymaker Fabled character, which gives evil players their usual information but the Demon must skip attacking one night. Ôªø

Does the Po choosing to charge satisfy the Toymaker's requirement that the Demon must choose not to attack at least once per game?

Yes.

Does the Poppy Grower ability still prevent the evil team learning each other in a small game with the Toymaker Fabled in play?

Yes.

If the Undertaker is resurrected at night (Al-Hadikhia / Professor / ...) does she learn the most recent executee, even if she was dead at the time of their execution?

Yes.

Does the Undertaker learn the role of an executed player that does not die?

No.

The Undertaker's ability reads "you learn which character died by execution today" so the execution must cause the player to die. So executing dead players or protected players means the Undertaker receives no info.

In a Riot game, does the Undertaker learn about all the execution in the day?

The ST chooses one of the executees for the UT to learn about, not all of them.

If a player is executed then swaps character (Pit-Hag / Barber / Engineer / Hatter) what does the Undertaker see?

They learn the player's role at the time of the execution.

The Undertaker's ability is past tense: they learn what character was executed, not what character that player currently is.

The poisoned Recluse is executed, but is not poisoned when the UT's turn comes up in the night, what happens?

The UT must see the Recluse. The UT evaluates the character not at the time that they wake but when the character died. So the ST has to take the answer at the moment of execution, which would have to be Recluse.

A player is executed and dies. Another dead player then breaks madness (Mutant / Cerenovus / Harpy). Can the second player be executed for madness breaking and shown to the Undertaker?

No, the UT learns which character died by execution. If one player is already dead, the UT can only learn the one who died by execution, not either.

The Imp is executed, the Scarlet Woman kills the Hatter, and the former Imp becomes the Spy. Could the Undertaker learn Fortune Teller?

No, they must see Imp. The Undertaker learns their character at the time of their execution, not what character that player currently is.

If the Recluse is executed, what does the Undertaker see?

The Undertaker can see the Recluse as any of the Minions, the Imp or just the Recluse.

The Undertaker can see the wrong role because roles like the Recluse and the Spy can misregister to other characters even when dead.

If the Drunk is executed, what does the Undertaker see?

The Undertaker is shown the Drunk character token, not the token for the Townsfolk that the Drunk player thought they were.

If the Spy is executed, what does the Spy see?

The Spy's ability allows her to register as good, even after death, so she could register to the Undertaker as the Spy, or as any Townsfolk or Outsider.

The Barber was killed by the Vigormortis, and swapped with a Minion. Does the dead Minion keep their ability?

No. A player must be a Minion at the time of the kill and remain a Minion the entire time for the Vigor to work. It is okay to become a different Minion, as long as they are never not a Minion inbetween.

If a player dies as non-Minion, they do not ever get to keep an ability even if they become a Minion later.

Killing the Evil Twin as the Vigormortis loses the unwinnable condition, because the text says 'good cannot win if you both live.' However, if the good twin is executed while the Evil Twin has their ability because of the Vigormortis, does evil win?

Yes.

What is the effect of the Vigormortis killing their Marionette?

Besides one of their closest Townsfolk neighbours being poisoned from now on, the Marionette retains their ability, but since this is a "you think are a good character" and killed good characters do not normally wake in the night, the ST should probably stop waking them.

If a living Minion gains another out of play Minion ability via the Plague Doctor, do they keep this second ability if killed by the Vigormortis?

Yes.

The Vigormortis kills their Pit-Hag. The dead Pit-Hag changes the Vigormortis to another Demon. Does the PH lose their ability due to the Vigormortis being no longer in play?

Yes. Additionally the ST still has a momentary ability to kill arbitrarily, so should probably signal the Demon change, because after that moment passes, the Pit-Hag's ability is gone again, so deaths are not arbitrary anymore.

Would a Vigormortis-killed Pit-Hag that turns themself into a Townsfolk/Outsider fail to gain that ability?

They would become that role and then no longer have an ability.

"Minions you kill keep their ability" means that if the person killed by Vigor is not a Minion, or stops being one, they lose their ability. Notably, a Vigor-killed Minion can be changed into a different Minion character and continue to use that ability, because it is still a Minion ability. But once they become something that is not a Minion, their ability is gone, even if they later become a Minion again.

If the Vigormortis-killed Poisoner poisons the Vigormortis, does the Vigor kill that night?

No.

The Vigormortis kills the Recluse who poisons their neighboring Townsfolk. Does the poison wear off if the Recluse is ever poisoned or drunk?

Yes. A drunk or poisoned Recluse cannot register as a Minion to the Vigormortis so the poisoning must stop.

Could the Recluse misregister as a Minion when she is killed by the Vigormortis in order to poison a Townsfolk neighbour?

Yes, this is completely legal. Also the ST could at any point choose to register the Recluse as a Demon or the Recluse to the Vigor, ending the poisoning.

Arguably Outsiders should always be used to hinder the good team, but the ST might need to consider game balance when making decisions.

Does the Vigormortis-killed Scarlet Woman become the dead Demon if the Vigor dies with 5+ alive?

Yes, which could end the game. Vigormortis and SW are not a great pairing.

If a Vigormortis killed Minion changes role (Pit-Hag / Engineer/ Hatter) does the Minion keep their ability?

A Vigor killed Minion keeps their ability and continues to poison the same neighbouring Townsfolk as long as they always remain a Minion.

If they ever stop being a Minion, they lose their ability and stop poisoning a neighbour, even if they later become a Minion again.

What happens if a Vigormortis-poisoned Townsfolk becomes a different character type (Pit-Hag / Barber) or a neighbouring player being skipped by the poison becomes a Townsfolk?

The target is no longer valid, so the poison must move to a new Townsfolk neighbour of the Vigor-killed Minion. This can still be in either direction from said Minion; reapply the poison to either of the closest Townsfolk neighbours.

A Vigormortis killed Minion keeps her power and poisons one of her neighbours. Could a second kill, by another character or by execution, of that Minion disable her ability and the poisoning?

A second kill would have no effect on the Minion: a dead player cannot be killed, they are already dead.

If the Vigormortis passes to the Scarlet Woman, do previously killed Minions keep their abilities?

No. It is a new instance of the Vigor and this Vigor is not the one who killed those Minions.

If the Vigormortis swaps players (Snake Charmer / Barber / Hatter ...) does a Minion they have killed keep her ability and continue to poison her neighbour, or do dead Minions need to be rekilled by the new Vigormortis?

Character swaps essentially reset the characters; they are replaced with new instances of the characters. In this case the Vigormortis that was giving dead Minions their abilities no longer exists, so those Minions lose their abilities and their neighbours become healthy.

A new Vigormortis cannot "reactivate" their dead Minions' abilities by attacking their corpses, because attacking an already dead player does not "kill" them.

If the Vigormortis is changed to another Demon (Pit-Hag / Engineer / Hatter), what happens to Minions they previously killed?

They lose their abilities and neighbouring Townsfolk are no longer poisoned.

Does an evil Apprentice or the Alchemist or a Townsfolk / Outsider turned evil (Mezepheles / Bounty Hunter / Cult Leader / Goon) killed by the Vigormortis retain their ability and poison a Townsfolk neighbour?

No, they are not a Minion.

If the Vigormortis becomes drunk or poisoned, do any Minions they have killed regain their ability when made sober?

Yes. It is a present-tense effect, so it is always in effect whenever the Vigor is sober and healthy. Ôªø

Can an evil Townsfolk (Mezepheles / Bounty Hunter / Cult Leader) still be poisoned by a Vigormortis-killed Minion?

Yes. The ability only checks whether the player is a Townsfolk; alignment and living status are unimportant.

If the Drunk believes that they are the Village Idiot, how many real Village Idiots can be put in the game?

There are only three Village Idiot tokens in the game, so if one of them is the Drunk, practically speaking there can only be two other Village Idiots, with one of them being drunk from their own ability.

If a player gains the Village Idiot ability (Philosopher / Cannibal / Pixie) could they be drunked by their own VI ability, gaining wrong info?

No, the drunking due to the VI ability is a setup effect. Also, gaining the VI ability does not make a player the VI, and the drunking specifically targets a VI. So, the info from the the gained VI ability must be sober, unless they are targeted by another drunking or poisoning ability or the ST house rules gained VI abilites otherwise.

If the drunk Village Idiot changes roles, do they become sober making one of the other VIs drunk?

They become sober because they are no longer an extra Village Idiot. They do not make another VI drunk because the drunkeness is a setup effect and cannot affect the middle of the game.

Can one of the Village Idiots be the Marionette?

Sure, if they neighbour the Demon or the Recluse. If this leaves one true VI in play then that one must be sober. If it leaves two, one of them is drunk and the other one is sober. The Marionette VI is then run like any other Marionette.

In order to guarantee the Marionette Village Idiot, an alternative setup of some sort is needed, such as substituting the Demon token in the bag with an extra Townsfolk, then on N1 picking a Townsfolk neighbour of a VI to become the Demon.

If there is only one Village Idiot, can they be the drunk Village Idiot?

No, only when there are two or three Village Idiots in the game is one of them drunked due to their ability.

Could an evil Townsfolk (Bounty Hunter / Mezepheles / Cult Leader / ...) trigger the Virgin?

Yes. An evil Virgin can be triggered too!

What happens when the Virgin is first time nominated by a Townsfolk protected by the Tea Lady?

The ST announces that the Townsfolk player is executed but does not die and starts the next night phase.

If a good Traveller nominates the Virgin will they be executed by the Virgin's ability?

No. The Virgin only cares if it is specifically a Townsfolk. Alignment does not matter. A Traveller is not a Townsfolk, so no matter their alignment it will not work. It will still waste the Virgin's ability though.

Is there another way that Townsfolk A nominates another player X and A becomes executed immediately, except X is a Virgin? i.e. are there any situations for X to simulate the Virgin?

i) Atheist game. ii) Breaking Cerenovus madness or Mutant madness while nominating could mimic that style of execution.

What happens when the first time the Virgin is nominated, it is done by a Witch-cursed Townsfolk?

ST choice:

  1. the nominator is executed and dies by the Virgin ability.
  2. the nominator dies to the Witch curse, then their corpse is executed by the Virgin ability. The ST announces "X dies and is executed".

In both cases the day will be over (barring the Butcher being in play). The first option hides the existence of the Witch, which depending on game state might be better for evil, but the second option makes the Witch a little stronger:

  • The Undertaker (who only learns about those who die to execution) would not be woken that night.
  • The Cannibal will not gain the ability of the nominator.

The Vizier's ability reads "All players know who you are." Is the drunk / poisoned Vizier still announced on the first day or can the ST make the Vizier believe they are sober/healthy by still announcing them?

The Vizier remains unannounced (and cannot force through an execution and can die during the day) until they become healthy and sober.

Droisoned players can never affect the state of the game, even if that means they immediately realize they are droisoned. Maintaining the illusion for that one player is less important than maintaining the basic principle that droisoned players have no ability and therefore cannot affect the state of the game. So, the ST may lie to a player that their ability is working but may not lie to the town as a whole that a player‚Äôs ability is working.

If the Vizier is the Lleech host, are they unkillable?

No. They are poisoned and have no ability.

If the Vizier is under madness and breaks the madness, is he executed?

You can execute them as the ST, but they would not die. It is probably a bad idea to as it just wastes a day for the good team with no counterplay.

If the Vizier forces the execution of the Lleech who obviously does not die, will there more be executions that day or not?

No, you have one execution per day and an execution will always immediately end the day (unless there is a Butcher) and there are never more executions after the first.

A player can be executed without dying, and there are some abiltiies that work interestingly around this concept. It is why the Mutant's execution instantly ends the day or why Cannibal specifies "recently killed executee" rather than just "executee".

If the Vizier is D1 drunk, does that drunkness mean that the Vizier does not have to be announced? Should it be announced N2?

Yes, and it would be announced the first time they are sober/healthy, same as the King. The how-to specifies the Vizier announcement is during the day, so RAW it is possible a Poisoner or other sources of droison could keep a lock on the announcement for a few days - similar to Leviathan but that is pretty risky if the Viz gets executed while evil is strategically holding off their announcement.

The Golem can kill the Organ Grinder but not the Vizier, correct?

Correct. The Vizier cannot die during the day for any means, unless droisened.

Can the droisoned Vizier die to execution?

Yes.

Does a sober and healthy Alchemist always have correct waking patterns in a Vortox game?

They are told the ability of an in play Minion but are treated like the ability they actually have, which would be the ability of an out of play Minion. So they have the wake pattern of their actual ability.

What does the Alchemist Evil Twin learn in a Vortox game?

Loads!

Firstly she is told wrongly that she has a different Minion ability, one that is actually in play. Next she learns the wrong role of another good player as her evil-aligned twin, which will likely alert her to the fact that she has the Evil Twin ability.

So she learns:

  • one of the in play Minions,
  • a confirmed good player,
  • the Demon is a Vortox.

What does the Alchemist, a Townsfolk role, learn in a Vortox game? / Is the Alchemist immune from the Vortox?

The Alchemist, although they have a Minion ability, is still a Townsfolk and is not immune to the Vortox. The Alchemist learns an in play Minion, but has the ability of an out of play Minion, as the Vortox causes misinformation but does not change the ability's working.

For example, in a game with the Witch and the Poisoner in play and the Harpy and the Devil's Advocate on the script, the Alchemist learns that they have the ability of the Poisoner while in reality they have the DA's ability. The ST still has to maintain the DA's restriction on not picking the same player twice in a row.

Would an Alchemist with the Spy or the Widow ability see an incorrect Grimoire in a Vortox game?

The Alchemist cannot have the Spy or the Widow ability as they are jinxed combinations.

In a Vortox game, the Alchemist has a passive Scarlet Woman ability, but thinks she has the Poisoner ability. Should she be woken every night?

No. It is not the same as a 'you think' like the Drunk or the Marionette who are constantly lied to. She should just got false information at the start, so N1 she is told an incorrect ability but then treated like she would be for her actual ability.

In a Vortox game, the Alchemist is told that they have the Godfather's ability (an information gathering Minion), when in reality they have a different Minion ability (say some passive Minion like Boomdandy or Scarlet Woman). What do they learn regarding Outsiders?

The Alchemist is just told that they have the Godfather ability, but then nothing else because they do not actually have the Godfather ability.

In a Vortox game, what does the Alchemist Godfather learn?

She falsely learns that she has a different Minion ability, that is in play. She is then shown out of play Outsiders.

Does the Philosopher Puzzlemaster guessing incorrectly learn the Vortox?

No, as guessing wrong already yields false info so does not need to be changed; the Vortox forces false info not flipped info.

Does a good player still learn the non self-poisoning Widow in a Vortox game?

Yes. The Vortox only affects Townsfolk abilities and the ping comes from the Widow, which is a Minion.

Are Townsfolk with a non-Townsfolk ability affected by the Vortox?

Yes.

Is the Duchess affected by the Vortox?

No. The Vortox affects Townsfolk abilities. The info source, the Duchess, is a Fabled so unaffected by the Vortox, even if it is a Townsfolk receiving the information.

Can the Lunatic learn true info in a Vortox game, this Minion is a Minion, the King is the King, ... ?

Yes, the Lunatic as an Outsider is unaffected by the Vortox falsifying of info. It is up to the ST whether this is a good idea.

What could the drunk Savant be told in a Vortox game?

Drunking and poisoning has no effect on the info received in a Vortox game; the Vortox forces all info to be false. The Drunk who believes that they are the Savant is unaffected by the Vortox due to being an Outsider, so their statements can be both true, both false or one true and one false.

Does the Monk protected player receive true info in a Vortox game?

Yes. They are safe from the Demon in all aspects, including secondary effects, assuming they are sober and healthy.

Who must the Monk protect for the Nightwatchman's pick to correctly learn the Nightwatchman in a Vortox game?

The Nightwatchman, because they are the source of the information.

In a Vortox game, the Nightwatchman picks a player, and that player learns someone else as something other than the Nightwatchman. The Monk protection can stop the Vortox from making info false, but in order for the target to learn the correct player as the Nightwatchman, it is the Nightwatchman as the source of the ability that needs to be protected when they use their ability, not their target. If the target is Monk-protected then the misinformation is not prevented.

Does the Philosopher Snitch and the Cannibal Snitch causes each Minion to learn three in play characters in a Vortox game?

Yes.

Townsfolk who gain an Outsider ability are still affected by the Vortox's falsifying of information.

What does the Vortox learn if the Cannibal eats the Lunatic or the Philosopher gains the Lunatic ability?

The Vortox learns the wrong player as their Lunatic and the wrong players for the Lunatic's picks.

How does the Pixie interact with the Vortox?

The Pixie learns an out of play Townsfolk. An arbitrary player is marked whose role does not matter. The marked player could in fact be a Minion, but probably should not be the Demon. If the marked player dies, the Pixie would gain the ability they were shown if they were sufficiently mad as that role.

How does the Pixie work when the Vortox is N1 drunk or poisoned and later sober and healthy?

If the Vortox is N1 drunk or poisoned then the Pixie will correctly see an in play character.

If the Vortox is later sober and healthy when the Pixie's marked Townsfolk dies, then the Pixie gains the ability that they saw, which if it is an info ability will be affected by the Vortox.

Does an evil Townsfolk (Mezepheles / Bounty Hunter / ...) still receive false info in a Vortox game?

Yes.

The Alchemist Fearmonger in a Vortox game ... does the ST announce that the Fearmonger has picked a new player?

Yes.

Public or even private announcements are not information. Only who is information for the purposes of the Vortox.

For example:

  • preached Minions still learn they have been preached,
  • exorcised Demons still learn they have been exorcised (they just learn the wrong player),
  • the Philosopher-Damsel would still inform the Minions that the Damsel is in play.

So the ST should still announce that the Fearmonger has selected a new player.

In a Vortox game what do Minions learn when they were chosen by the Preacher?

That they were chosen by the Preacher, same as a non Vortox game, as being told that you were picked by a player is not part of the vortoxable information. If it were an ability where you learnt who picked you (such as when the Exorcist picks the Vortox) then that would part would be falsified.

How does the Nightwatchman ability work in a Vortox game?

The target of the Nightwatchman / Philosopher Nightwatchman / Cannibal Nightwatchman / Pixie Nightwatchman wakes up and learns that they were picked by the Nightwatchman but is shown the wrong player.

The Vortox says Townsfolk abilities yield false info and info passing characters such as the Nightwatchman are ruled that the ability name/type is not part of the vortoxable information - "someone with the NWM ability chose you" is a mechanical explanation of why someone woke up, and [ST points to a player] is the information.

Does the Soldier, who is safe from the Demon, correctly learn the Nightwatchman if picked in a Vortox game?

No. The source of the information is the Nightwatchman and they are not safe from the Demon.

When a player is D1 executed but does not die, the Undertaker does not wake, but does the Oracle wake to learn whether it is a Vortox game?

Yes.

The Philosopher picks the Damsel ability in a Vortox game. Do the Minions still learn the Damsel is in play?

Yes.

Being targeted by an ability (Damsel, Nightwatchman, Exorcist, Preacher, King, etc) is not falsified in a Vortox game, though any information that goes along with it would be (in the case of Nightwatchman, Exorcist, and King that is the learning of a player), though that does not apply to Damsel (even filtered through Philosopher), so they just simply learn the Damsel is in play.

If in a Vortox game that contains both the Damsel and the Philosopher Damsel, what do Minions learn?

Minions learn that the Damsel is in play.

Being woken due to an ability to learn affected you or is in play is a mechanical aspect not affected by Vortox; only learning specifically who is.

Consider similar interactions in Vortox games: A Minion that is selected by the Preacher is still told that they have been preached. If the Demon is picked by the Exorcist, the Demon learns this but learns the wrong player. The demon learns that the King is in play, but not the correct person.

The Magician Vortox interaction... does it work the same way as Philosopher Lunatic in a Vortox game, where the Demon learns a wrong name?

No. The Magician already gives false information because she appears as a Minion. So, with a Vortox or with another Demon, there is no difference.

Does the Noble have to see all good players in a Vortox game? Or can they see 2-3 evil players too?

They can see anything but two good and one evil. Including all evil.

Is it possible to learn true information in a Vortox game due to a character misregistering? For example, can the Empath who should learn a zero when they neigbour a good player and the Spy registering as good, instead learn a one in a Vortox game?

Yes. It was previously thought not, but since the ruling that the Fortune Teller's Red Herring yields a "no" in a Vortox game, the majority (but not universal) view is that this generalises to other kinds of misregistration, including the Spy's.

Does the Grandmother's grandchild have to be an evil player in a Vortox game?

No. The Vortox'd Grandmother has to learn one of player and character wrong for their grandchild. They can learn the right player wrong role, right role wrong player, etc.

Notably, they do still have a good player as a grandchild and will still die if that player is killed by the Vortox, because that is a mechanical effect, which the Vortox cannot falsify.

Is the Gossip affected by the Vortox?

No, the Gossip is not considered an info role.

If the Vortox dies and the game continues for whatever reason, is the Vortox ability now nullified and thus all information reverts back to being true, barring droison?

Yes. Since players lose their ability when dead, then the Vortox's ability of forcing false Townsfolk info is no longer in effect.

Would the Alchemist Pit-Hag in a Vortox game make people learn the wrong character? Or is that not 'information'? What about the Alchemist Cerenovus? What about Minions that make a public announcement like the Vizier and the Fearmonger, would the ST announce incorrect information?

Learning your character and alignment is never "information" for the purposes of the Vortox. Learning what character you are mad as is not information.

In a Vortox game, does the ST lie to the Amnesiac about their guesses?

Yes. For example, if they asked if their ability was to do with voting and it was not should you still give them a warm/hot?

If the Nightwatchman is in a Vortox game, the player chosen will be shown anybody, but the Nightwatchman, including a Minion. If the Preacher chooses a Minion in a Vortox game, does the Minion get the info their ability stops working or not? Is it a Townsfolk ability yielding false info?

Being told one has been chosen by an ability does not get falsified with Vortox, so a Minion would learn they were chosen by the Preacher. If it is accompanied by learning a player, such as in your Nightwatchman example, or also, for example, Exorcist, then the player shown must be false.

What do the evil team learn if the Poppy Grower dies in a Vortox game?

Because the info is coming from a Townsfolk ability it must be falsified, then RAW each evil player must be told incorrect info.

The ST can show the Minions and the Demons only good players, but evil Townsfolk, if there are any, can be shown.

More specifically team red must learn non-Minions as Minions and non-Demons as Demons, so as a workaround Minions could learn another Minion as the Demon and, if this is a 2+ Minion game, the Demon as a Minion. The Vortox will still have to learn non-Minions as their Minions but they will at least know that their info is wrong.

What does the Knight learn in a Vortox game?

The Knight learns two players one of which is the (or possibly a) Demon.

In a Vortox game, what should the Fortune Teller get when they hit their Red Herring?

They would get a "no".

Can the Recluse create true info in a Vortox game? For example the Chef sees the Recluse as evil, so sees a pair where there is no pair, so learns there is no pair, which is true information despite the Vortox.

It was previously ruled "no", but since the Vortox/FT ruling came out most people would say "yes".

The FT's Red Herring can cause them to get a "no" when they choose the Red Herring but not the demon (and a Vortox is in play). It has been controversial, but the concensus is that this implies that the Vortox can flip information after accounting for misregistration.

How does the Bounty Hunter interact with Vortox misinformation?

They learn a good player. When that good player dies, they learn another good player. Even if the Vortox is killed, droisoned, etc., the BH is only shown a new player after the death of the shown good player; the BH never gets their information corrected.

The BH is shown a player and they will only ever get a new name when that player dies, regardless of that player's actual alignment.

Is the Apprentice immune to the Vortox due to being a Traveller, or does their Townsfolk ability still yield false info?

Travellers get true information in a Vortox game. An Apprentice getting info from a Townsfolk ability is not a Townsfolk player, they are a Traveller player.

Can the Fibbin cause a Townsfolk to get true information in a Vortox game?

Yes.

If the Fool does not die by execution for the first time, does it count as a succesful execution for the Vortox?

Yes, any execution will satisfy the Vortox's condition, even if it does not lead to death.

How does the Vortox affect the Balloonist's information?

Each Balloonist reminder token is placed next to a character that is not that character type, so the Balloonist basically just gets four arbitrary names.

Note that the four names the Balloonist learns cannot be one Townsfolk, one Outsider, one Minion and one Demon.

What do you tell the Savant in a Vortox game?

The Savant is given two false statements.

Does the Vortox learn of the King or the Exorcist?

The Vortox correctly learns that the Exorcist / King are in play but always learns the wrong person.

D1, a Minion is executed while the Minstrel is in play, so the Vortox is drunk. If on D2 no one is executed, does the evil team win?

ST choice; it could go either way.

Two actions that occur at dusk would attempt to happen at the same time:

  • At dusk tomorrow, all players made drunk by the Minstrel become sober; the ST removes the EVERYONE IS DRUNK reminder.
  • Each dusk, if no player was executed today, the game ends and the evil team wins.

This is an order of operations issue. Whichever happens first loses the interaction.

One interpretation: The Vortox will be drunk until dusk. The day ends with no execution, then dusk happens, so the Vortox is still drunk at the point they otherwise would have won. They do not become undrunk until that start of the night phase. The game continues.

Alternative interpretation: First the Minstrel's tokens are removed, then we check the Vortox wincon. Evil wins.

Given that the Vortox was drunk up until literally that moment, arguably it makes more intuitive sense that they would fail to win the game.

Can the Washerwoman see two village idiots?

Yes.

Does the Widow know which good player is told that they are in play?

No.

The player is decided after the Widow makes their choice. Also there is no knows token for the Widow to see in the Grimoire.

When does the Widow get to poison in a Poppy Grower game?

After the PG dies and they see the Grimoire for the first time; they do not get to poison blind N1, not even themselves. This means that the Widow announcement is guaranteed to go out on their first night.

Does the Widow get to see first night information reminder tokens when they view the Grimoire? For example, if the Washerwoman was going to see the Soldier, should those tokens be placed before the first night, or directly before the WW step; is that information that the Widow gets to know?

Anything that looks at the Grimoire sees what the ST has in there. Most STs choose to leave those tokens in, but they technically do not have to.

If the good player who knows the Widow is in play turns evil (Cult Leader / Mezepheles / Goon), and the Widow still has their ability, does a new good player get pinged?

Yes, a new good player is woken and shown the Widow character token.

The Pit-Hag creates the Widow. Does the Widow see the Grimoire that night or the next?

That night; it is their first night, so they should be immediately woken and shown the Grimoire.

Note that the Widow is not an info role that must wait for poisoners and killers to act first. They have a mechanical ability that lets them see the Grimoire and poison someone as soon as they come into play.

If the Widow is created mid game (Engineer / Pit-Hag / Hatter / ...) when does a good player get told?

A good player learns of the Widow that night.

If the Witch cursed player tries to nominate an already nominated player, do they still die?

They should not die, as the nomination is not valid. However mistakes happen, so if the player mistakenly nominates and then the ST were to mistakenly act on the Witch curse, the best solution is for the ST to admit there was a mistake made, apologise, and continue on as best they can, with the player dead. The ST could ask if they would like to nominate someone else instead but they are staying dead regardless.

What is the Exorcist jinx with the Yaggababble?

If the Exorcist chooses the Yaggababble, the Yaggababble ability does not kill tonight.

If the Scarlet Woman says the Yaggababble phrase and then the Demon is executed, is their a kill?

They could cause a kill if the ST gives them that phrase, but they are a new instance of the Yaggababbale so they could also be given a different phrase and not cause a kill.

Does the Scarlet Woman become the Demon after the Zombuul dies for the first time?

Yes, so there will be two acting demons, which makes SW and Zombuul a bad combination.

If the Zombuul neighbouring the Tea Lady dies for the first time, do they register as the TL's neighbour?

No.

If the Zombuul is registering as dead and there are only two other players are alive, does evil win?

No, the Zombuul registering as dead does not count for evil's win condition.

If the once-killed Zombuul is drunked or poisoned, does the game end?

No, the game continues because importantly the Zombuul has never actually died. Their death shroud is not removed and nothing is announced to town. They no longer register as dead for roles like the Tea Lady and the Oracle that care about living status.

If the Zombuul that has not already died once is killed while drunk or poisoned, what happens?

The droisoned Zombuul dies for real even if they have not used their extra life.

If the Zombuul loses its first life, would an Oracle's number rise by one?

Yes.

In a Zombuul game, if a dead player is executed again, would the Zombuul wake the following night to kill?

Yes, the Zombuul's ability checks whether a player died, and dead players cannot die.

The first time a Zombuul is executed, do they still wake at night to kill, if no other player dies that day?

No, their "death" registers even to their own ability so the following night they do not wake.

If a dead player becomes the Zombuul (Pit-Hag / Hatter / Engineer /...) do they return to life as a once-killed Zombuul?

No, they are the genuinely dead Zombuul.

It is only the Zombuul's ability that allows it to misregister as dead that gives them a second life, and dead players do not have abilities unless specified otherwise.

Is the once-killed Zombuul who either swaps with a Minion (Barber) or becomes another Demon (Pit-Hag / Engineer / Hatter) just the dead version of her new character?

No, she is alive but remains appearing as dead. Nothing in the ability prompts the ST to announce anything about her life/death status since her status has technically not changed. As a result the town do not know to flip her life token back over: in person, the town square is maintained by the players, not the ST, and online the ST simulates what the players would do.

From the players' perspective nothing has changed, but abilities that care about living status are affected: she does not register as dead, so abilities can see, choose and impact her.

The Zombuul does not mix well with character changers; it is kind of awkward no matter how it is run.

Does the "dead" Zombuul have a ghost vote?

Yes.

Can the "dead" Zombuul vote more than once?

After their first vote while registering as dead they would lose their ghost vote. Mechanically they can vote again but voting more than once while appearing dead would out them, so probably a bad idea. Some STs would rule that the Zombuul cannot vote again and would not count any ghost votes after the first.

The Zombuul is executed. Then, the Engineer picks another non-Zombuul Demon from the script. How does nominating and voting work for the former Zombuul?

When the Zombuul dies for the first time they:

  • are given a death shroud,
  • have one dead vote for the rest of the game,
  • register as dead,
  • cannot nominate, and
  • do not count towards the majority needed to execute.

When swapped, the former Zombuul

  • still keeps their death shroud but
  • can vote freely,
  • no longer registers as dead,
  • can nominate,
  • affect the number of votes needed to execute

As soon as they start nominating and voting freely they are outed, so they probably do not want to do that. The number of votes needed for execution could also tip off town that there is a fake dead Demon somewhere.

What happens if the Zombuul registering as dead is drunked or poisoned?

There is no immediate visible effect. They are not announced as alive so the town square, which is the players' responsibility, is not updated.

But they no longer register as dead to any other abilities. For example, the Empath and Tea Lady abilities would no longer skip over them. Whether they can now be deliberately targeted by abilities that specify a living player (Chambermaid) as their target is debatable, as this strays into the trying to cheat area.

The number of votes required to put someone on the block changes, which may tip off town to the drunk/poisoned Zombuul being in the game. Some STs decide not to alter the number of votes in the case of the drunk / poisoned Zombuul.

If the Pit-Hag changes the Demon to the Fang Gu, could an arbitrary kill of an Outsider count as a Demon kill causing a jump?

If the Fang Gu chooses to kill an Outsider, the ST can allow that to go through. Otherwise players the ST chooses to kill are killed by the Pit-Hag, so no Fang Gu jump.

If the Pit-Hag creates a Fang Gu and the arbitrary kill at night kills an Outsider, can that cause the Fang Gu to jump?

If the Fang Gu themselves targeted that Outsider, the ST can choose to allow the kill to go through and thus the Fang Gu to jump. The ST can also choose to block the Fang Gu's choice of an Outsider and have them die to the Pit-Hag with no jump.

Or, of course, the ST can block the kill entirely and not kill the Outsider to either ability.

If the Fang Gu did not target an Outsider, they cannot jump - if that Outsider dies, it is only to the Pit-Hag's ability and not to the Fang Gu's.

The Pit-Hag turns another Minion into the Fang Gu. The new Fang Gu targets an Outsider. As deaths are arbitrary tonight, is the jump blocked, or is it legal to kill off the old Demon, and allow the jump to happen, killing off the first Fang Gu and the targeted Outsider becoming the new evil Fang Gu?

Each Demon's choices are still taken, which the ST does not have to abide by, with any arbitrary protections or deaths occurring from the Pit-Hag.

It would therefore be valid for the Fang Gu‚Äôs jump to be processed as per usual, with the newly created Demon dead and the Outsider converted, on top of the arbitrary death of the original Demon.

However, it would not be legal to kill the Fang Gu and have some other random unselected Outsider converted instead.

In full, the ST's options are:

  1. The Fang Gu kills the Outsider, so the jump happens i.e. the normal Demon kill goes through; any other deaths are due to the PH.
  2. The Fang Gu does not kill the Outsider, so there is no jump and the Outsider remains alive i.e. the PH's "deaths are arbitrary" ability
  3. The Fang Gu does not kill the Outsider, but the Pit-Hag does, so the Outsider dies but there is no jump i.e. the PH's arbitrary deaths ability

If the Pit-Hag creates the Fang Gu and then the Fang Gu chooses an Outsider at night, and the ST allowes his kill to go through, does this also make the Fang Gu jump? Does the kill come from the Pit-Hag's ability or not?

Either. The way Pit-Hag arbitrary deaths works is that the ST can block any kills (or not), and can cause new kills originating from the Pit-Hag. If the ST allows the Fang Gu kill to go through, it jumps. If they prevent it but then kill that player anyway with the Pit-Hag ability, then there is no jump.

If the Pit-Hag changes the Demon into the Fang Gu, can the Fang Gu jump that same night? Does the Demon's choice matter at all that night or, because of the Pit-Hag's deaths are arbitary ability, are all deaths caused by the Pit-Hag instead of the Demon?

The ST can allow the Fang Gu to jump.

..ST's options are as follows, assuming the new Fang Gu chooses an Outsider when deaths are arbitrary:

If the new Fang Gu targets an Outsider then, since deaths are arbirtary, the choices are:

  1. the chosen Outsider is PH protected and does not die;
  2. the chosen Outsider is PH protected and does not die, but then is PH killed, so no jump;
  3. the chosen Outsider dies to the Fang Gu, so the jump happens.

"Deaths are arbitrary" means the ST can allows deaths go go through, or not go through. So if the ST allows the Demon's choice to go through, that one is an attack from the Demon, not the PH, and if the ST blocks it, then it is treated similarly to the player being protected from the demon that night. Any "additional" deaths are considered attacks from the PH.

Can a drunk or poisoned player gain true info from their ability?

Yes, unless it is a Vortox game when their info must be false.

If the Courtier drunked Demon makes a choice, then the Courtier dies by a Gossip that night, does the Demon's kill go through?

No. The Demon was drunk at the time their ability would have fired, the malfunction means no reminder token would have been placed, so at no point was anyone marked to die.

If the Harpy is drunk or poisoned, is their target still informed that they were targeted?

If the Harpy was drunk or poisoned at the time they picked, no, as their ability has no effect.

If the Preacher was drunk when he chose a Minion, will that Minion be preached when the Preacher becomes sober?

No. Mechanical abilities used while drunk have no effect on other players.

If a player that wakes at night is drunk or poisoned, could the ST just skip them?

No, drunk / poisoned players are never skipped. The ST should deceive them that their abilities are functioning normally, otherwise it would confirm to the player that they are either drunk or poisoned.

Reminder tokens are placed/removed regardless of drunkenness or poisoning:
  • a drunk Juggler will still place "correct" reminder tokens,
  • a drunk Gossip will still place its "dies tonight" token,
  • a Minstrel will still place its "everyone drunk" token, etc.
The drunkenness/poisoning simply disables the ability that makes these tokens do anything. So what happens when the normal flow of an ability (place when needed, remove when checked at night phase) is interrupted, such as by droisoning or by a character change?

A more broad rule of thumb: If the player was drunk/poisoned at the time of their ability then a token is not placed, and if no token is placed then it cannot "come back."

If a token was placed and that is interrupted by drunk/poison and then the drunk/poison goes away, then the effect of the token comes back.

However, backward looking roles are run differently, with their tokens placed down for the ST's benefit. Abilities like the Juggler, Gossip, Mathematician, Town Crier, and Flower Girl have reminder tokens that essentially do not actually take effect until the night phase and putting them down during the day is just to make the night easier for the ST. That is why the ST still tracks them, because when the info/mechanical part of their ability truly goes off, they need to know in case the character is not drunk/poisoned. It does not matter if they were droisoned when the tokens were being placed, as long as they are sober and healthy at the time they get their info, it will be correct. Conversely, if they were sober and healthy when the tokens were placed, and droisoned at the time of getting their info, the info is arbitrary.

In a Poppy Grower game, the Vigor-killed Poisoner poisons the Vigormortis. What happens?

Endless drunk/poison loops are resolved by having all parties drunked/poisoned, until one effect wears off as it normally would. In this situation, both the Poisoner and the Vigor are poisoned, and the poisoned Townsfolk is temporarily healthy while the Poisoner remains poisoned.

The Marionette has a special case for when the Preacher picks them that their ability stops working and the ST pretty much ignores them at night since thinking they are a Townsfolk is their ability. Could the same logic apply to the Drunk or the Lunatic being poisoned or drunked? Or would that be too powerful and against the never reveal the Drunk unofficial rule?

With drunkenness and poisoning, the goal is for the ST to still pretend their ability is still working, which for the Drunk / Lunatic means still pretending that they are the character that they think they are. So drunk and poison are not very similar to being preached.

Are there any characters that can make players sober and/or healthy?

There are:

  • A Barista one can make another player sober and healthy for the night they are chosen and the following day,
  • The Beggar makes herself sober and healthy at all times,
  • The Monk can protect from/remove a Demon's poisoning for one night (No Dashii / Pukka / Lleech / ...).

Can the poisoned Demon kill people?

No. Poisoned characters have no ability.

What would happen if someone who is drunk gets posioned?

No real difference as they do the same thing. They do not stack but it is still important to track both in case one ends before the other. They are sometimes even used interchangably as "droisoned"

Poisoned is similar to drunk right?

Poisoning and drunkeness mechanically work the same. If an ability makes a player drunk or it makes a player poisoned, it has the same effect. So, information is arbitrary and mechanical based abilities do not work at all.

Being drunk and being poisoned are technically different for the purposes of Savant statements and Artist questions, although usually those would involve saying "drunk or poisoned‚Äù to catch all cases.

If the Poisoner poisons the Minstrel, and the Poisoner is executed, is there a Minstrel night? Same for Widow too. Does the poison wear off before the Minstrel sees that a Minion died?

This is a question of simultaneity, and there is no official answer. A valid interpretation is that at the moment the Minstrel sees the Poisoner as dead, they are not poisoned (because the Poisoner is dead), so the Minstrel procs.

If a character that is drunking or poisoning someone is changed into a different character, does the droisoning stay?

No, because the ability that caused the droisoning no longer exists.

Examples:

  • If the Imp self-kills and the Poisoner becomes the new Imp, then the Poisoner is no longer in play and is therefore not poisoning anyone.
  • If the Pit-Hag turns the Philosopher drunking the Savant into the Mutant, then the Philo is no longer in play and is therefore not drunking the Savant.
  • If the Pit-Hag turns the Puzzlemaster into the Klutz, the previously Puzzlemaster-drunk player is now sober.

If a character is poisoned, they become healthy if the character that is causing them to be poisoned no longer has an active ability. How does this apply to a Snake Charmer, or does it not?

The SC poisoned by another character would become healthy if the other character was drunked, poisoned or dead. If the SC poisons themselves, infinite poison loops are resolved by applying the poison.

Can poisoning reapply? If a Courtier chooses the Imp but is poisoned on the second night of their ability, is the Imp sober or drunk on the third night of the ability?

If droison would be applied while the character is themselves droisoned, it is not. If the ability was applied while sober and healthy, the reminder token is flipped upside down, the target is temporarily sober/healthy and when the droisoner regains their ability, it continues to apply. So in this example the Imp is made drunk once again for the third night of the Courtier's ability.

If the drunk or poisoned Philosopher uses their ability to gain another ability, and later gets healthy again, do they have the functioning ability of their character of choice, or did they never use their ability?

Any once per game ability used while drunk or poisoned is spent, the Philosopher is no exception: their attempt to aquire an ability does not work and spends their OPG ability and, for as long as they remain droisoned, the ST should pretend the ability they received works, but once they are healthy the ST can no longer deceive them.

In a reverse scenario, if the Philo was sober/healthy when they picked (so they gain the ability) but then became droisoned they may receive false info or their mechanical ability does not work, until they are sober and healthy again (when the ability will resume functioning normally). While droisoned the ST could even stop waking them up and pretend they were poisoned at the time they used their OPG ability (but if they become healthy, they would have to start waking them again).

What if the Philosopher is sober when they choose an ability, but they are drunk when they use it?

They have gained the ability. While drunk/poisoned, they may receive false information or a mechanical ability does not work at all. When they are sober/healthy again, they go back to working normally.

If the Philosopher is drunked or poisoned, does the Philo drunk player become sober?

Yes.

Can there be more than one Demon in play at the start of the game?

Only in a Legion or a Riot game.

Can a multi-kill Demon attack the same player twice? e.g. the Shabaloth tries to eat the Fool twice with both kills, or the Al-Hadikhia chooses the same player three time, thus ensuring they die?

No, it must be different players.

What happens when a multi-kill Demon (Al-Hadikhia / Po / Shabaloth) picks a protected player?

This will likely depend on the source of the protection and the order of the Demon's picks.

If that player is protected due to their own ability (sober Sailor / Soldier) then they cannot die no matter who else dies that night.

If the protection is due to another player (Tea Lady / Innkeeper / Monk) then that player cannot die, as long as source of the protection remains alive. This means who and the order of the Demon's picks is important:

  • If the source was not selected by the Demon, the protected player cannot die.
  • If the source was selected after the protected player, the protected player survives but then the source, barring any other forms of protection, will die.
  • If the source was selected before, then on their death (which includes choosing to die to the Al-Had), the protection is removed, and the target of their protection is no longer safe.

In the case of the Al-Had, if all three players choose live, or all three are alive at the end of their choices, then all three die in the order that they were selected. Again, the order of death matters: the protected player survives if the source of the protection was picked afterwards (or not at all).

If a multi-kill Demon (Al-Hadikhia / Shabaloth / Po) kills two players where the first killed player was drunking the second, is the drunking removed before the second kill?

Yes.

The order of the kills is important: as long as the player causing the drunking dies before the drunked player, then the drunked player becomes sober.

For example, the Philo-drunking is removed if the Philosopher dies before the original of the character. So if the Philo-Ravenkeeper and the Ravenkeeper both died in that order on the same night then they would both get sober info.

Can Demons choose dead players?

Yes.

Demon bluffs ... what is allowed / recommended?

The Demon should be shown three characters that are safe for her to bluff as, to avoid double claiming a good player. These characters should:

  • be any combination of Townsfolk and Outsiders; two Townsfolk and one Outsider is pretty common,
  • out of play
  • not be Minions; bluffs must be good characters

It is strongly recommended that whatever characters the Drunk or the Marionette believe themselves to be are not given as bluffs; although out of play, the Demon might not appreciate receiving these! Additionally, some STs would consider it illegal to do so; the argument is that the Demon should see three out of play tokens. But if the group is experienced it could be attempted, perhaps to signal to the Demon who the Drunk is.

If the Demon changes player (Fang Gu / Lil' Monsta / Imp / Snake Charmer / Pit-Hag / Barber / Hatter / Scarlet Woman / ...), what do they learn?

They learn:

  • what Demon they are;
  • that they are evil, if they were previously good.

Additionally the are told if applicable:

  • the King,
  • the Marionette,
  • the Lunatic, along with any picks they make each night.

The Marionette, the Lunatic and the King are all "the Demon knows who you are" abilities, so the new Demon learns any that are currently in play and active that they have not already been informed of.

The new Demon does not learn any bluffs or the Minions, as this info was given in the Demon info step which already happened, unless it was skipped because of an in play Poppy Grower, in which case all Minions and Demons learn each other when the last sober and healthy PG ability dies.

The Philosopher N1 takes on the ability of an out of play character. Since the Philosopher's turn comes before the Demon gets their bluff, is it correct to say that the Demon cannot get the role the Philosopher took as a bluff, since that role is in play?

The Philo's pick has no affect on Demon bluffs. The Philo only ever gains the ability, she does not turn into the character, so the character remains out of play.

Any character out of play on setup can be given as a bluff, and if the Philo chose one of those bluffs then it is just unlucky for evil if they do not pretend to have poisoned info.

The Philo is before N1 evil info just so that she can take the Poppy Grower or Magician abilities which would affect evil info.

If the Demon is drunked or poisoned N1, can he get bad bluffs?

No, because getting bluffs in not due to the Demon's character ability, and so cannot be disabled by poisoning or drunking.

Do the Demon and the Minions learn each other's role during the Demon and Minion info steps on N1?

No, just they just learn who is on the evil team, not specific roles.

In case of the Cult Leader starting a cult, are all good players supposed to vote including the dead players, or only the alive ones?

Including dead players. Cult forming (like exiling travellers) is not a regular vote. Dead players are included and dead votes are not used. Abilities that specify executions (e.g. Flowergirls) are not triggered. An organ grinder is not triggered. Only votes for execution count as votes for abilities per the glossary.

A call to exile a Traveller, the Demon votes. Is the Flowergirl informed?

No. Exiles are not executions: They do not require or use a vote token (and, as such, require the normal full majority), do not end the day, and do not interact with any abilities that specify executions.

Does the Flower Girl read the Cult Leader votes as well as votes from nominations?

No, the Cult Leader does not use votes, only raised hands.

If someone dies during the day (Harpy / Tinker / Witch / ...), does this change the number of required votes, and can this put people on the block who were previously safe, having just gotten not quite enough votes before those players died?

An execution requires the majority of living players to vote and to have the most votes of the day.

So players dying can lower the number of votes required but

  • any nomination still needs to have more votes than any other in order to put someone on the block,
  • there is no impact on nominations that have already happened - whether someone is on the block or not is determined immediately in that moment, and any previously safe player is still safe.

For example, if player X gets five votes and that is not enough and then people die and five would be enough now, player X is still safe, and another player would still need at least six votes in order to be put on the block.

Does a resurrected player get a ghost vote if they used it while dead the first time?

Yes, each time a player dies they get a ghost vote token.

Can someone die (due to the Tinker, Slayer, Cerenovus, Harpy, .. ) during a vote? Must it wait until after? It feels like active abilities might make sense to be paused during a vote, but is this an official rule?

Yes, players can die during a vote, nothing really stops that... on a practical level, it is unlikely for the Storyteller to do as they are busy spinning around in a circle counting votes.

Would you allow the evil team to openly and loudly communicate their plans during the night phase in crucial game-winning moments?

Sure, there is no rule against it.

What can players say during the night phase?

You can say whatever you want but with a few exceptions like not narrating what actions you do at night or saying that you did not wake up till the morning after. But if you want to give someone advice what to do at night based on info that was known the previous day absolutely do that, or as a minion lean over to your demon and tell them who they should kill.

Player A is made mad that player B is evil. Another player suspects A is mad and asks her to prove if she is mad or not by saying something that could get her executed for breaking madness. Would saying something like "I am mad that player B is evil" count as breaking madness, despite her keeping madness the rest of the time?

The ST should not consider this a madness break.

Player A is doing that in an attempt to convince the town that they are not mad, and the intent and sincerity of their madness is still retained. Intent matters a lot more for madness than the words someone says.

The group might want to address this issue together as asking someone who is mad to break it to prove that they are mad runs against the spirit of madness.

All madness related abilities, except for Pixie, are phrased with "might" to stop the evil team from exploiting forced executions from the Cerenovus and forced deaths from the Harpy in ways which go against the spirit of the characters. With the Mutant the "might" is used to ensure that it functions as an Outsider by making the execution happen at an inconvenient time for good.

If a Traveller is turned evil (Mezepheles) are they shown the Demon?

No, only Travellers who start the game evil learn the Demon.

If the Traveller Goblin claims Goblin while they are executed, does evil win?

No, as exiling is not executing.

Can dead players call for a Traveller to be exiled?

Yes.

Can Travellers be made mad by the Cerenovus or the Harpy?

Yes.

And while Travellers cannot be nominated for execution, the ST can execute them for breaking madness.

Are there any character abilities that can influence whether a call to exile a Traveller succeeds or not?

Yes:

  • the Tea Lady ability works on all good players including Travellers
  • the Apprentice Vizier cannot be exiled
  • the sober Apprentice Sailor cannot be exiled

Does the Apprentice Psychopath play roshambo if they are exiled?

No, an exile is not an execution.

Where on their home scripts are Travellers on the night order?

All of them act first if they act at night except for the Apprentice which will act at the turn in the night order of the ability she has.

Does a Traveller being drunk or poisoned have any influence on them being exiled?

Only when their ability would normally have saved them from exile (Deviant / Apprentice Vizier / Apprentice Psychopath).

Can Travellers nominate?

Yes, they are treated the same as regular players.

In a game with multiple Demons (Legion / Riot / ...) what does an evil Traveller learn?

They learn just one Demon player.

If a good player is babysitting Lil' Monsta are they still seen by an evil Traveller?

Yes.

If a Traveller joins the game is their role immediatelly known to everyone or is it secret?

Everyone knows what Traveller they are for as long as they are a Traveller.

Can Travellers deadvote?

Yes, after exile they have one dead vote like other dead players.

Can the Pacifist save a Traveller from exile?

No. The Pacifist can save a player from dying to execution, and exiles are not executions.

Can the Devil's Advocate save a Traveller from exile?

No. The DA can save a player from dying to execution, and exiles are not executions.

If a Traveller breaks Cerenovus madness, would they be exiled?

No, they would be executed ending the day.

Do Travellers count as players for end of game? If there is a Demon, a good Outsider, and a Traveller left in the day, is the game over?

No, Travellers do not count towards the end of game player count. The example situation is a game over. Travellers do not count towards the living count for final three purposes. Travellers do not count for the win condition.

Do Travellers count for the purpose of evil's end game condition of surviving to final two?

No.

For example, if a Traveller, the Demon and one other player are left alive, then evil wins.

Do Travellers count for the King's ability?

Yes, same as with votes, they always count for the total player alive number except for evil's win condition.

Do Travellers count as alive players for the Chambermaid ability?

Yes.

If a Traveller voted on a nomination prior to their exile on the same day, does their vote still count?

The votes for a nomination are immutable as soon as they are recorded by the ST.

The Exiled Traveller's votes prior to their exile still count for that day. An exiled Traveller is still in the game, they are just dead. and they have one vote from the time they died, the same as any other dead player.

Does the Demon learn if a Traveller who has just joined is on their team?

No, the Demon never learns the alignment of a Traveller. An evil Traveller, however, does learn who the Demon is, so they can go ahead and tell the Demon as much though the Demon may not believe them - they could just be good and fishing!

What happens if the Apprentice Philosopher Snake Charmer chooses the real Demon?

By default, nothing, because normally a Traveller cannot become a non-Traveller, which makes the Snake Charmer a poor choice for the Apprentice. However, if an optional rule mentioned in the rulebook that players can become Travellers and vice versa is used, then the Apprentice would become the Demon and publicly lose their Traveller status and the Demon would become the Apprentice, which everyone would know and ultimately makes Snake Charmer a poor choice for the Apprentice. A good example of why Apprentice is recommend for Bad Moon Rising and not Sects and Violets.

Can a good Traveller become a Farmer?

Under standard rules Travellers cannot change characters so an alive good Traveller cannot become a Farmer. However, if the variant where this is legitimate is used, then when a Travaller becomes a Farmer their life token in the town square is changed from a Traveller one to a standard one.

Do evil Travellers learn the Demon in Teensyville?
